et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not go too far in the foundation, so you do not cover the foundation that holds the ground, and comes out by the way of nature;
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then the physician, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	in case it should heal, or you remove that covering and clean it up well from the foundation, or by stretch or by any other tool;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then mix that wood in the wound as well as you can;
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	then study to restore the wound, and hold back the fistula in the opposite part of the foundation: it is lighter work for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And there is no place for fistulas according to this method: and when you stick the tent into the fistula, and it is where it touches the base of the skin above,
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	if one takes a tent pierced at the top according to this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	and I stick .i. wire in .ij., and stick the tent on all the wire in the fistula as long as it is at the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is persisting in the margin inside, then remove the wire from that one, so that you stick your two at the base;
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	and train the head of the shaft, and bring together the .ii. shoulders together, and hold apart, and leave it .i. day or .ii..
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and do not restrain at any time, until the rope has passed between those two, and they are chafing;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then heal the wound as long as it is souded and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, if you can pierce it in all ways that you can, unless it is too completely enclosed.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not right to do for the lameness if perfect, and then heal, as we have said, until he is healthy.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The form of the spatemile with thorns that one makes a fistula is very hot and painful; therefore it is not possible to make it perfectly well without great pain.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	On the other hand, one must not do what one cannot do; for one must not do what one can do. For this is not right to do for the lameness if perfect, and then heal, as we have said, until he is healthy.
des emorroydes	of the hemorrhoids.
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	1 Emorrydes are according to these manners: or they are at the bottom of the foundation, also as a grain of resin, and there are small ones and great ones, and cut close together,
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	2 and one or more of them are at the bottom of the foundation and at the top of the foundation; but those that are at the top have little moisture, and those that are at the bottom have great moisture, and those that are in the middle have moderate moisture.
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	3 and then cut a little of the yellow water or a little of the blood, and they have the color of the body; but those that are at the bottom have great blood, and those that are in the middle have moderate blood.
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	4 and the cure for those who are at the bottom of the foundation, so that you command the patient to sweat in bed as long as the foundation is hot, and they discover the filth; but those that are at the top have little filth.
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	If you are in a hurry, and hold it like a claw, then cut it at its roots;
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the nail falls off because of moisture, take it with a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of chamois leather;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and remove them with your fingers, then cut them off, and powder them with hot powders that are in the fire's place;
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you can cauterize them as described in the chapter on cautery, then treat them with other treatments until they are healthy again;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if his foundation cannot come out, let the patient be clistered with a hot and harsh clistre to wash out what is in the foundation so that it can come out freely;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	Let the patient be bathed, and if his fibers are firmly attached to the foundation, then the cure is light;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and you shall press them with your nail or with tweezers, and cut them off, then heal them as we have said, until they are well, and do not incise them with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	If it is necessary that you bring the stitch according to this method: take a twisted thread, and put it in a needle, then turn the thread over and over on top of the needle, and pierce the needle from the other side, and twist the two ends of the thread together behind the needle.
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and if it is large; then hold the thread in place, and tie the knot, and remove the needle, and do the same with all the others, and leave it. i.e. to stop the excess blood;
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then put on the foundation. i.e. dip in oil or wax, and put it on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest;
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then leave it until it has passed wind, and when it has defecated, if the patient is cured of anointing and other cures, until he is well.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	and finally on the foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is drying up of the bowels from nature, and when the disease is old and medicine is not effective.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	If you cut off a spur or your fingernail too high, leaving it exposed to moisture;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	and then treat it until it is hard again as it should be;
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot harden, then shave it more closely than before, until it bleeds and is scorched;
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat as long as he is healthy.
dou fremit	he perspires.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	Here comes the translated text:
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and it does not burn his throat, and you can hear it as if he were dead, and it spreads throughout the whole body, and more in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure is that you take a feather from an ostrich, or a strong vulture's feather, and put this feather on the pulse, as long as the purple circle covers the pulse entirely.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand on all the feather as long as you cover completely the pulse, and put it in place, and scratch the pulse from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, make a wound of a feather of rain or iron according to this form, and be subtle and run over it:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce, so it does not hurt, but press And if you see, cauterize the pulse, as it is in front or chapter of cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the cloth
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	No once made is the cloth of silver or bronze, or of melted gold or brass; and no once made are these small or great instruments, according to those that they are to be used.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	So once made are those for the cure of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the cloth is small and large depending on its width, or the belly is tied according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and I say there is a rift where the belly is tied together, so that you see it, and where the legs are within the cavity, and on one side there is an opening of 12 inches, and on the other 1 inch.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and let the belly be where one puts medicines from a bladder of best wine or parchment, and let it pierce all around the smaller openings,
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and between each opening let there be 1/4 of an inch of space, then bottle in these openings strong thread of twisted rope in 10 or so threads around, and put together the belly as if it were a sheep;
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicine is inside, if the lid is placed in front of a strong tool, then make it into a ring; and that is the shape of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and oil the head with olive oil or almond oil or a similar substance, then pour it lightly.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	Then the ministers hold it together with their two hands until it is completely warm, then remove the oil and place the patient's legs against the wall.
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	Then let the medicine be poured out on the patient, as much as he can bear; and if he sleeps a whole night, it is greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cauterize with fire due to disease of the stomach, and the medicine is poured out quickly, then it is too much for him if he is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are at the fundament or the abscess, then also the clister is too thin like a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the form of the clister, thin as skin, so that the skin is stretched:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken in the division of the cure of wounds; now we will tell you the cures for hands and medicines, according to accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made of, and according to the places where they are made, and for this reason they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by the impact of a stone, and the cutting of a sword or a dagger, or an ax, or a spear, or a sledgehammer, or similar things; or
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or where the heart is struck, as a wound on the neck, or on the head, or on the chest, or on the belly, or on the liver, and similar limbs; or
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, for the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound occurs or the head comes first, and the bone is not broken, if you take care to look for movement of stones or similar things, then the skin is often torn and the wound is large.
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you doubt the warmth of an abscess: if it is too soon to know for certain whether it comes from a wound or not in the head itself, but rather if it comes from a wound at the opposite end from the part that was injured;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and keep the patient away from wine and thick meat.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	and if he does not sweat, if his meat is not reduced, and if he does not drink wine or eat cheese.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and wet the wound, if a blister forms, soak it in oil or wine with astringent;
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no blister, if it is placed on the wound, if it is fresh and not moved by the air, powder, which I will mention a little later;
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the air has moved it, place some onions on it until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together by tension, bring them together with sutures, as I will say for wounds in the belly, from the stitch.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is exposed to bone and blood, and holds only for a little while, then heal the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	And instruct the patient to eat large meat, as tested and baked wheat, also like poultry, and similar foods.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find putrid flesh on the skin, and it does not reach the bone, then chop it all off, and burn it up, and then heal it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if he has an artery in the wound or vein, which, without stopping, and it cannot stop with medicine, then cut the artery, and if you find it dislocated, so that it is a thread;
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if he does not benefit from it, then cautery.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the light cure is: and that you put this powder that hardens so that fire moves it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the way of the powder is this: take incense one part; dragon's blood .ij. parts; live fire .iij. parts, and the powder finely,
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and apply the wound, and the bandage forms, until it is well dried up and joins all its blood;
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then bind it well, and leave it unbound if it does not swell, for one should not bind the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never does one use salt at all, unless one has dragon's blood and fire oil, but the arm should not move the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the arm has moved the wound, most certainly it is infected, so one must put this powder on it;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put on some distilled water and honey, or bread made of barley flour, until it heals;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let them grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold them steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	For if the bone breaks with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine tweezers;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you later about the breaking of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound on the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	The wound comes from the neck and is simple, if there is no difference between it and that of the chief, but the neck where the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the case, if there is no other obstacle to the healing process but to allow the wound to heal naturally and put nothing on it that might hinder it, for it hinders healing and makes it retreat;
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything on the wound, for the substance of the neck is cold, and its course runs with the brain, which is the highest member;
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	however, if the medicine is like warm water mixed with oil and rosin, and washed with lukewarm water;
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other stones according to this method, and wet oiling.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, so that the bandage is not enough, then heal until it is well.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and full of bowels and blood, and the hole or lower down;
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut, and the flow of blood comes from it, if the darkness and fever come, and the cauterization is done;
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	and if he sneezes from his throat, or coughs, and the wind is kept back, so that the meat goes forward.
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	if the cough goes up the throat lane, and does not touch the throat but returns it to its natural state;
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then he is left a few days, and is cured of garlic-based remedies as long as he is healthy;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then it is wanted;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are pieces of bone, if you can't carry them all, and those that you cannot bring, leave it until the wound is rotten.
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and let the issue be dried up and firm;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle on the powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and there is a fistula, then treat it as I have said in my chapter on the ointment.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or a sword
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it is a wound from a lance or a sword, and the wound is deep, then examine the wound to see if there is wind coming out of it. Know then that the wound is fatal;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it is not deep and the wound is fresh in every part of it, then do not put the powder on it at all, nor bind it up so that it does not heal completely;
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and turn your attention to the patient and watch over him closely;
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but I met an attractive omen, and lay down. ij. times a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you have no omen, put cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture,
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and let the patient sleep on the wound for .iij. days, or more often, or many times;
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if there is no spasm, nor a strange trembling of the heart due to the fire cautery;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see the good arrangement, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Heal the burns and other wounds, as long as they are healthy;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it cannot heal, and a fistula forms, then know that it is necessary to operate, as should be done.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a knife or sword, and it is simple, or on the front or back, then know how to heal that one.
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	s'elle est grande, de couture ; et s'elle est petite, de poudre, et s'elle est pressée en l'os, et en a copié des pièces, si vous voulez la plaie, et les traiteras fort s'ils sont déséquilibrés;
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not dislocated, let the wound fester, and so will be the extractions.

dou derrompement dou ventre	and the rupture of the womb

Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second way of sewing, which Galien distinguished properly,

de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula where it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	knows that all wound or abscess, when it heals, is called universal "fistula".
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and most often when it has healed and the bowels have moved.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And the fistula is according to the theory of the nature of the tissue tough and white, and one does not feel pain there.
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and is also like a bird's feathers;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	nor is there ever clear rain, nor thick fog;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	neever poking, and sometimes enough;

ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	It is due to one of these .viiij. causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	it is due to the small blood or pus;
ou por sa malice;	or because of their evil nature;

ou il i a voinnes ou os:	"Or if there are veins or bones:"

Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	It is known that fistula occurs in all limbs of the body.
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	because there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves,

et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if you see the fistula clearly with your own eyes, take a piece of leather or iron and, if the fistula is straight, feel it;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if its fistula is twisted, so the search for a thin rope of plunging.
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	for the plunging turns to the curvature;

car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	For moisture is short from one hole to another, and cleanses it.

ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	Here is the translation of the provided Old French text:

Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve is injured in the main members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if his eye is uncovered and there is corruption and blackening, if the king holds out until the corruption is entirely bone,
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then the treatment of things that are ruined, as much as he is healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if he is not healed, and returns bowing as before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	for you are not yet able to move:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	and if you stay in bed and rest
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and then restore the joint;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if he is thus sound, then it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	if not, know that the corruption is too perfect, that you cannot come to him;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other means than to be easier by nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can pull it at the claws,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	if you extract with an instrument suitable for this.
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if he has several bones, if they are twisted, do not leave more than one in place;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if moisture makes it contrary, and there is no mistake or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	if you cover and moisture and heat, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, put on the wound something that prevents infection.
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and leave it so that the hair grows around the bone.
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then the bones will heal more easily.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a large bone, such as a leg or thigh
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	if you have only this corruption as long as the blackening is all bone,
puis restoure la plaie;	and then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large part of the corruption, and it comes just to the edge of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if it comes to cover all the way up to the corruption, and then cure it until it is sealed;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you may take an example and aid in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	There was a young man aged xxx-xx years who had a pain in his leg due to an internal cause that originated in the core,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	as matter came out of the leg, and was escaped by a large abscess, and had no apparent cause to open it;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but he stares at them because of his madness so much on that the abscess opens.
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and in corroding with matter they become a fistula, and I came out of a hole so great that all was bowing and moistening the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many miraculously healed in .ij years, and there was no skill in this art of hands.
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	as long as I was called, and I saw a leg and the medicines that he was cured with,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and who runs through the openings with great speed.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and his body would turn red when he ran, and had an orange-colored skin.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I set up a tent in one of these openings, and then searched for all the openings
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and I found that one came together with the other on both sides of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I was hurrying then, and I hit on one of the holes as hard as I could until I uncovered a part of the bone.
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and I found it腐敗したそして壊れていた、そして腐敗は骨の中まで来ていた;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I knew what had happened to the bone, and I took care that there was no other corruption except for that which I found;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to heal the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, and it could not be healed;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I began, and uncovered the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and I found the continuous corruption in the bone, and softened it, and then I held it, and leaned down to weld the place.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not as much as cup my hand around one end of the bone, and I pushed it forward with all my might.
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	and then I treated it with medicine; and it was healed and firmly welded together,
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and do not wish to recommend the work for anything but the weakness of the disease, which cannot be borne.
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and from the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For with blood loss there was often, but he was completely healed, and
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and gave birth to a hard mass of bone, and was of good temperament and had no harm or contrary in all things, nor did it affect his breath or coming into being.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if his nose is broken at any place under the heart, then it shall be done thus:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	Take .i. a thread, and draw out to the head of the bone that is broken,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and command any one who extends it upwards,
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and put another thread of a larger size than the first thread around it and tie it above the joint that is dislocated,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and let the head be, so that you take the cart rotted on the ditch,
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the cart on top of the ground where you see hay, so that the hay does not damage the cart;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and place .i. kindling or a pile of straw over the cart to cover up the rotted cart;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary as much as you can see and feel the corruption, and sometimes also;
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if his nose is corroded, and does not open any more, and the corrosion is in the middle or in a part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	then uncover the chest completely; then put on .I. a hot coal,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then tie one part of the corruption to the other with silk, and let the silk be long from the corruption .I. piece, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corrosion is in the joint, then disassemble the joint corruption, and tie the bone or what it contains on the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if corruption occurs in the continuation of the twenty-one joints, there is no other pain than that of the cup.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if corruption occurs when it is poked with a hand or when it is poked with a foot, this is very strong.
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but you must also inquire about the corruption, how it hurts you.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and wash it in all ways that you can, but let the vein or nerve not hurt you.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the incisor and the sutures to cover these bones are many, according to the shape of the bones and the appearance of the teeth.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and fineness, and their size and smallness, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for each kind of work there is an appropriate tool.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that the work will teach you the tool you need, according to the knowledge of this craft.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the ways of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if you use the instrument that is right for this.
dou feu	dou fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head may be dislocated due to cold or due to heat;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have medicine which is corrupted by the treatment of the medicines, and it does not benefit at all,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	it is necessary to cover that member until the place where the corruption comes;
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the patient escapes from death or from the evil which is greater, from the failure of the member;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the members become black, and that they seem to be burned by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and then after the blackness, then goes those corrosion of member by member,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and seizes all the body; if you hurry to cover it,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it is by the percussion of some venomous creatures, like a sea scorpion or a weasel and similar things,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	the corrosion is at the head of the two, if it covers, and does not give space to come until the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, so that the cup does not reach the joint, so that the corrosion does not come up to the arms.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes to the arm, so that the cup reaches the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, it is death,
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there is no need for a test of its strength except for the quantity of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and completely stop it when the corrosion comes at the foot: if it comes to the first joint, so that the cup is after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to stand, so cover all of the foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it rises in the leg, so cover at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, so there is no other danger to the patient but to die;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the way to cover or sew the member so that you tie it above and below,

et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you displace the bar that is between the .ij. lines to .i. spadille wide, until the bone is uncovered;

et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and bring to the patient other wound and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if the blood flows out when you work, then cauterize it well.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	Or put on some powders that restrain it; then return to your medicine as long as it is completed,

et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you that there was once a wise man in some town:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	He had a darkness that seemed like fire burned.
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and this corrosion came first in his two feet, so much that it stained all the foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	And when the honourable man saw the corrosion, he took off all the copper from the foot, and was healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long after that, the corrosion returned to his two hands, and came to me;
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put him on reflective things after purification of the body, and cannot stop the corruption;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he said that I should cut off his hand, and I do not say, that I had hope of reflecting on the substance;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would not die;
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	For the virtue of the man was weak; and he despaired completely, and returned to his country,
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he held his arm away from the copper pot, and was healed.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have told you this only so that you may do something else if necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	There comes one time when incising a lump of flesh, and delays so long that it makes great assembly of bowels;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then it rips and piercing, and springing the bowels, and staying the viscera, as our vassals;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the leather that is above it is also as soft as... drape-leads untied,
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and do not cut it until you reach the bone, nor until you hit the nerve, and such a disease is called "healthy".
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	is not called "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it becomes so long that it reaches the bone in perfect proportion, then it is called a "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the cure is that you wrap this wound very tightly, and especially when it is thin, as with a scarf.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and do not wet it for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have promised that the leather will be dried, and the corruption is not complete,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the leather is hard like a wheel, if the cure of the cloth is thus:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	regardez si ses seins sont gros, et le bouton qui en est fait a un odeur puante,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	therefore the egyptian medicinal enema which is made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take oil and alum and equal parts of lime, and put it to cook in a 1/2 vessel on the fire,

et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and in the cauterization of the breast, and extract the stone;

et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine makes the blood sharp.

Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bow is complete, if it does not leave a trace.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the loins so as to see,

car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	For when the bow is complete, if it does not leave a trace.

Des vils	The vils
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	The vile vis are huge, enveloped, filled with superfluity of melancholy, which come from many members of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and more is found in the legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry loads, while others
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It therefore comes that you do not give any spurring of horses, and then the health of the bazaar.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;

Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The size should be according to this manner: raise the first leg with hot water very strongly, until the large veins are thin.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	Then strain the sick leg from above the knee down to the shin;

et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then let it rest, and instruct him to dye his meat with black wine;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and then begin the evacuation and sweating when the veins are clear, and nurse the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	Here is the translation of the text line by line into English:

De la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in the legs, in warm places where there are no herbs or trees, and in the earth where there is no moisture;

Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of worms that come between the skin and the hair
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our country "buffalo disease," because it often affects buffaloes.
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a little worm that was born between leather and saddle, and goes all over the body going up and down.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and it smells good when it goes from limb to limb, until it rips the leather where it went, and jumps far.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is covered with pus of some humors, if it comes towards and coils and twists and worms or insects that come out;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and one doubts its maliciousness, because when it goes through the body, and it goes up to the head, and it comes out at the mouth,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	for fear of entering, and destroying the oil; and such things have often happened.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it cured and drained, so can one only do it when it is:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	So that it may be done with a strong ligature tightly tied,
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then cut off above and below it, and dip it into boiling water, and you will not find it.
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	If the fire cautery, as long as he dies.

et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see the head coming towards the oil, then hold back the spell with your hand, then cast it away and leave it.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and use a bad medicine to clean out the harmful odors.
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and are made sick with putrefaction of meat.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	from pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that affects certain members,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and moves from member to member; and I saw the one I told you about.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to see a sick woman, and she uncovered her breast, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of her breast.
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and then I saw it grow like a worm in her shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	faster than anything else, it seemed to me to be alive and shining as silver when it cuts from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain departed from the affected area, and settled in her shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little later corrupted throughout the whole body, as it came to the other breast;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then he told me that she twisted all over the body again, as I saw her.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled at how she moved from member to member, for I have never wanted such a disease in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Nevertheless, I have seen many people who, when they had pain in one place, felt it in another.
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I do not want it, if as I saw in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that this was because the woman had a dry chest and open veins,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and for this reason does she seem so wind-blown and constricted;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and it does not appear to these people who are delightful, who have moist chests and relaxed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see this disease healed, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	If the wound is cleaned and bandaged well, and then it is covered with a cloth so that the wind does not blow on it.

si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if the cure of this disease, if like pills that are rotten, and pills of serapin, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various, according to their appearance and according to the places from which they come.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of them is that there are some with great points, and small, and curly, and welded;
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those that have .ij. angles, and those that have tongues, and those whose pieces are separated;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and those who are injured in any limb so long as they are not injured according to .ii. manners: or if the limb is injured in principle,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	as brain, heart, liver, pancreas, kidneys, intestine, bladder, and similar limbs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When she is injured in any of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	if it is necessary for you to remove the arrow, for death comes after a number of preparations;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this bad sign does not manifest itself to you, and if the arrow has not been fully extracted, then turn it over, and heal the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	and the sign of the skull when the arrow catches and pierces the bone, and the surgery that is on top of the skull,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when cutting and turning and twisting and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of speech, and vomiting of food;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps it is a loss of smell or hearing; and perhaps it loses its speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and salt from the wet wound that looks like pus, and also as if it were burned with fire;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and this sign will warn you, if you keep the cure, and remove the arrow if it is not embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it pricks or hurts, is that it is near the left breast, and also as if it were stuck in something hard, not hollow.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and the arrow might also be like a bird, and in black blood, and cold sweat comes and faints:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	And so there is doubt of death.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that does not have a poison is that there is no foam coming out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's color changes, and he breathes heavily and trembles with fear.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow enters into the shell of the chest, then the small ribs ache; and there is great pain and sorrow and breathing; and all the limbs move with a tremble.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow enters into the stomach, perhaps there is no foam coming out of the wound, indicating that it has entered into the digestive tract and caused a disturbance within.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow enters the belly, and there is no hope of cure or extraction of the arrow by the route it took through the intestines.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow enters the bladder, and urine flows out in spurts and the patient feels great pain, know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member - if it is the face or neck or throat or shoulder or arm or spine or leg or foot, and similar things - are safe according to many considerations.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow enters a nerve or artery, and it is not poisonous  - as I will tell you about my own experience - then do otherwise.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	There was once a man who had an arrow stick or lance, or something like that, at the root of his neck;
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and tore off some of the fat from the ear, and was cured without a trace of pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I tore off a stick that was in his neck, cutting through some of the fat from the oil with a paper knife,
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the stick was returned, and I only felt a pricking sensation on my finger.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and this arrow is great of a turquoise arc, that is to say, it is lighter than the ears; the game was sound, and there came no bad accidents.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And shot an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and this arrow was Arabic to the ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I let them grow beards, and I hid them until they were shot, and the Christians remained sound.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I shot an arrow at a man, which was an arrow of death, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then let it pass for .xxx. days, unless it changes its condition;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut off the arrow and extracted it, and tied it tightly, and I did not leave a bad mark.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if there is a hole in one's heart where an arrow has passed through, and the wound is closed over;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and let the arrow rest within it, and do not change its natural state,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	There is no harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And I see another man, to whom an arrow struck in the face and was seared;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And it stayed there suffering great pain; and many others.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And he threw an arrow at the king of the nobles, who was hit in the eye with an arrow.
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and there was one declining to the right side; and the arrow was completely embedded.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to treat it after it had been shot three days earlier. I found the wound to be very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I treated it with a strong substance, and did not feel it at all;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt tingling and pain in his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought that it was from the tip of the arrow
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on him the plaster of the attariffic digestive, so that his legs do not swell;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I felt his legs from the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put on him the plaster every day, and quickly heal the wound, and prolong the life of the patient.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	as long as he feels the arrow .i. inside his body; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put on the wound a corrosive aqueous medicine by hand, as long as it was open,
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I tried it, and felt the tip of the arrow which was fixed in place;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I applied to the opening of the wound the corrosive medicine, as long as the tip of the arrow was clearly visible;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and properly define the terms before .iiiij months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then stretch it if the wound that I put the pliers on, and pull from both sides, and cannot get out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	then I stopped from subtlety and devising of tools, until I took .i day with well-made pliers,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to this person whose form will come at the end of this chapter of chalk, until I stretched it, and brought back the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And I tell you, the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored.
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Or you have said the quality of extraction of certain arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you put your cure on those which I do not say, for the books cannot take all into account;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but the master healers compare a very small number of things, and on those that are present and weakling.
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	true there are nine works, and nine instruments, for the removal of foreign matters which come in this craft.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not come from the limbs except by the following nine ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or through the place where they enter, or through another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and those that go out by the side where they enter, are arrows going into their flesh, and do not go out at any time nowadays.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not go out now, let it stay until the flesh is rotten inside, and the exit is cured;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And if it is stuck in the bone, and cannot come out, let it stay like this for some days, and change it every day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then let it go out, and if it does not go out, let there be a small hole everywhere inside the flesh, as long as the inside of the leather is wide, and then treat it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the skull, and goes just to one of the ventricles of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have said to open the patient: if you do not draw it out, but leave it until it is even after a few days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	For if the arrow comes just to the sinews, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is lodged only in the muscle, and goes just to the sinews,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and let the patient stay for some days without any bad accident, if the machine of pulling.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very badly broken and cannot be taken out, then administer hot tar as I told you; then cure the joint until it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is reinserted into the neck of the body so that it cannot be seen, and one seeks it with all one's strength;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, and if you treat it with any suitable tool;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot by stretching out the wound, and because of the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if there is no bone, nerve or vein, then the wound must be very large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and train the arrow if you can, and if it has ears to hold it in place,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	so that the bone is broken at one of its ends, where the arrow is lodged,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or rain the ears of the arrow, as long as you can pull it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and carefully try to break the arrow, so that you might pull it out with more pain.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it once, then take it back to the place where the arrow is located, and try again, for the extraction is painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the pain of the extraction makes you faint, then administer what we have said in this chapter about the cure with its ointment.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and to guard against injury to the nerve and the vein, and place it so that you can remove the arrow without danger;
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	or is dried or cooked well or firmly or thoroughly; and place the patient in accordance with the form he was in when the arrow entered;
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	For this is the greatest aid that there is, and if you cannot do that, then place it according to what your sign shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from elsewhere, where it opens nothing, or the leather is swollen in place so that it can be seen or felt apart:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Therefore, cut it off as long as the jaws can take hold of it, and then extract it: if not, do so now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	If it is held in the bone, turn your hand roundly as long as it enters into the bone and widens it, then remove it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	If it cannot be extracted, let it go for a while, and then begin the extraction again as long as it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if there is an arrow in it, shoot it out completely.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if he has a fever, and you see that it is not administered, then administer it with an instrument made of wood,
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the point of the arrow enters into the wood of the instrument; and then pour out,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is cut, pour out the instrument with the point entering it, to rejoice in the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow touches, so that you cut all the cart around where the poison is, if you can,
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	and then treat the wound as he thinks fit.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow is in the neck or back or bladder or ribs, and it is close, and you can cover it, then you cover it; if you don't,
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and beware of covering the vein and nerve, and then extract it, and then cut the wound, that is a job.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it is well.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the pliers used to extract arrows is like an eye, and here is the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the pliers for cutting hair is also like the feathers of an owl, and here is that form:
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	For in order to cut the tip of an arrow, as it is in this shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of pliers for gripping and for holding so as to be:
des voinnes dou cors communes	common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	The veins from which one heals are: xxvi., from which there is a head of xvi.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	This is a medical text in Old French, and the line you provided translates to: "It is known that: .iij. batans (veins) which are after the ears, which are called the 'douz herbech'."
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the 19 arteries that are in the 19 temples appear;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the 19 veins that are in the 19 arms of the hairs, which are called "aspirates";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is in the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the head;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the 19 veins that are at the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the .ij. veins that are in the lips above the mouth, and these veins are called "augerich";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the .ij. veins that are on the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins that are commonly talked about are .v. in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	the one is the cerebral, and it lies on the left side of the body, and it is called by the lay people "voinne du chef";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the pain is called "fast", and is composed of the cerebral and bazal.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and they call it "vein of comfort"; and the bazal if it is on the right side,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and they call it "vein of the belly", and is in the light.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and this is the one that is heard, which opens clearly on top of the chest.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the little finger is the vein between the thumb and the index finger, and if it is at .ij. inches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and where the foot are .iij. veins: one is at the edge of the pocket of the left cheek,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein that is called 'nesse', which is in the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg are .iij. veins beside those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The pain in the veins that are behind the ears, if it is helped by the ancient catarrhs, and migraine.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the qualities of the disease, as I have told you, are that you remove the head of the sick person,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the spot where the veins are with an abrasive cloth; then hold the neck of the patient with a vise,
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	while the .i. veins appear behind the ears in .i. two lines depending on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	Here is the translation of the text line by line:
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	"Then take the lance and pierce through the vein until you hit bone, then lift your hand up to where the vein emerges from the upper arm."
