et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	"And cut and bind the flesh and the vein very carefully. Make two cuts through the skin and the vein, and then pull it away from the meat as much as you can see."
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	"Then stretch and tie it, so that it is healed."
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said the incision and cauterization of the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The two arteries that are in the two temples, if it is old Migraine,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and headache, and blindness used to be, and in the eyes tears;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of the patient is so as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and let the patient strip his neck until the veins appear clearly.
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and put on a poultice of ash and then sign with salt;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	and then apply hot poultices to your chin and neck; and then take a needle and thread, and tie it tightly around the vein at the top of your index finger, and cut the thread,
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and then cut the vein above, and tie it up, as you did in the other 15 veins, and make a hole with your finger according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	and then lay down the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then let it form, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of their treatment and extraction, or the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The healing of the vein at the forehead is as effective as the healing of the facial diseases of old, and for headaches and torments.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is that the patient twists his neck until the vein appears.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	and take the instrument which is called 'trowel', whose form is this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And put the point on the vein, and hold it with your hand, or another thing, and let out blood according to the quantity that you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then cut off the neck of the patient, and tie up the vein until it is stable, and never use a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, the flame must not be too hot; and the vein is cut across, because the bone is close by, and the flame may break when it is thin.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The saint blood that is in the two veins of the face, help with hair, and with scrofula, and with redness, and with the oil of the ear, and with diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of his blood is that the patient should pull out his tongue by twisting it with no chain, as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then he shall suck blood, and let his blood flow a little from the tip of the flame, a little wide, because there is no fire.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if his flame is thin, by chance if it is broken; then he shall make the blood run, as much as you need, and then he shall lay it on a cotton wool, and he shall lay it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The sick person of the birth pangs is worth water, and also sudden fever, and diseases of the face.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	such as migraine and pain that comes in the face, and even when it is old.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the quality of the sickness is such that the patient twists his neck, then pulls his navel towards his left hand.
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take a long, subtle flame, and put it in the space between the i-ith nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	For the vein does not open well now, and the blood will begin to flow soon.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not apply too much heat, and let the blood flow according to your need, then leave it for a night, because it is soon restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	are the seven principal diseases:
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of health is that the patient extracts his hair from both sides, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and the master standing over the head of the patient, and the patient cuts with .i. scissors,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then cut the vein from the long side a little widely, then tie up the blood vessels temporally, or as much as is necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then make another in the other vein, then loosen the knot, and extract the blood vessels gently,
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	that the patient does not choke; and leave it until morning so that the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	Of the healing of the limbs
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	Of the healing of the mouth and its ailments, including gingival problems, lip defects, and mouth ulcers and their treatment.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the qualities of this healing are to have the patient sit before you, and to hold his neck as I have described.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	and turn the lip, and look at .ij. veins, one is on the right lip and the other is on the left
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and know by this that they are black, and by this that there are small veins near them that are black:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	then know both of them, and if you do not know them, and if you are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	then choose the larger of the two, and do likewise with the 2 veins that are above and below, for this is a similar way.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the heat of salt water, the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	Of the heat of salt water, the tongue so helps after the heat of the head, and it is to the extraction of the throat, and the diseases of the eye, and the diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the doctor is that the patient dies between your hands before the sun, and he lifts up the tongue, and looks in each side a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	So then heal one and the other, and do not become too perfect, for the veins are black.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins which are commonly treated are done so according to .ij. ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	where cut with sharp flame or small oil droplet, and is called 'aneil'.
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide and thin according to the width and thickness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame is named as it is, and is wide as you see it:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is a skill to open the veins that are thick with blood, which is evident and troubled.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtle in point, and it is to save the subtle veins, where there is subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The cure for the basilic, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases of the throat, collar, chest, and abdomen;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the surgeon to wash the wound, and to bind up the artery that is severed.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he stops the artery, and blood comes from the cut, if it is necessary to stop the blood flow, as I said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and should not be struck with fire, but cut in a way like this.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the base is not clearly visible, then it is necessary that you extract it and change it.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	If you see any bleeding from it, or if you feel pain at its base, you will need to cut into the vein in order to save the arm. It is clear.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and hold the fire to the wound, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you can see the site of the injury, then it is necessary to extract the arm, touching the site until you feel the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	Then mark the site with chalk, and then cut the arm off, holding the fire to the wound.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and beware that you do not wound in the artery when you see the edge open, for it is in the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	and if you see coming up above as urine of a child, and the sap is red and thin, know that it is sap of an artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	then hasten you, and put your thumb on it for a long time, then open your thumb so that the sap comes out, for this often happens;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	lie down, and leave it alone, and do not move the patient; and be afraid, and do not move him until he is well.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if he does not stop bleeding, and the medicine is not present, if you cut the artery, for the head of the retort stops it; stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take an bark of fennel, and cut it, and take one of the halves and tie it well until the other day;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If he stops bleeding, it is good; if not, use the powder that stops blood, as we have said,
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stopping of blood is not done in many ways for the small size of the wound and the ability of the vein of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The blood of a vein is to be drawn when treating with the head of a staff, and the base of the neck.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	for it is composed of the bazille and cephalic, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and the surgeon must be careful of the nerve that is exposed, and if he cuts too much, it will split the nerve;
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells and the patient's health is compromised, and perhaps it cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any man by its subtlety, then you must take away the tool from him; and avoid this nerve to your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then cut it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The healing of the cerebral wound with fire, so that it is attracted to the head and held in place;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to heal with fire the wound of the cerebrum, because it is attracted to the head and held in place; and it is necessary to use olive or tin flame, for it is the most healing of all the veins, since it does not destroy the nerve or artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	But nevertheless, it is necessary to seek the lighter cure first, and do not worry if one fails at first time, and start again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance the limbs of some men swell up, but it does not matter if it fails the first time, but there is no harm in that.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health is as you think it is.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you should know about a healer is that healing should only be undertaken to maintain health.
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to prevent the diseases from coming.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and let the surgeon make the cut in one of the three veins that are located on the head, which is to say, the cephalic, facial, and basal vein;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and the surgeon must prepare in advance by fasting for three days and in autumn and winter after eating, when the sign of fullness appears;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and the surgeon must prepare on the first day or third day, after 2 hours or 3 days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The saint who is free from disease has no fixed fever, but whenever he needs to eat or drink, at all hours and in all seasons.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And it is not necessary to keep the children until they are .xxiii. years old, and women except for four months until the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	And it is not necessary to sanctify those who have passed the age of .lxi. years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when any one is sanctified, in whatever way it may be, if it is necessary that he defile the entrails of a light clister,
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	s’il a mouth of fins retained, so that the veins do not attract the intestines the superfluities porries harmful to the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	not heal at all those who are too sunburned by meat, nor those who are drunk, as much as it is necessary, nor those who drool;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and so heal after a colic passion, and vomiting, and stomachache, and multiple childbearing, and sleeping, and fasting, and this all the virtue, or by a weapon or the heart;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	and then subtly the humors, it is thick outside, by meat and by drinkings and by medicines, if you have any doubt about it;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	and between or bath, if anything offends him, for subtilely offend him blood.
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and heal the wound from within by the third, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and protect him from work, food, lust, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be tied and jointed, and be higher than he who heals him, and rub his arms .ii or iii times,
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then remove the ligature by means of a slight pull, for when it is too tight or loose he cannot run without;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the wound with his hands, until the veins swell and can be felt;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	and then soak the wound with a little of old oil, then put his thumb of his left hand on that vein for a moment or two;
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not run and does not bleed.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that run like strings, and if they are such that they are easily winded up,
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	So that when one puts it on fire, if one takes it off fire, and cannot open the vein, then it is of this type;
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if one opens the vein, if the wound is too tight, so that the surgeon must be warned in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened for the first time, it is good; but if not, if it begins again after a while either on the field or in hospital, if the injuries are inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if his arm is swollen, and the patient expects, let him stay .i. day or .ij., and do not tie up his arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	So that the abscesses may come out; do not go into a bath, but begin to sweat if it pleases you;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	And if his fracture is small, or the pain subtlety and you doubt that it will not be as much pain as you see, so firm in this fracture right to all flame;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And work a little hospital, so that the arm is swollen; for this often happens, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the wound open, then don't put salt on it, but put a little oil on it, for it softens the course of the blood in this wound and is moisten by this oil that lies there.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and then apply the oil to each wound that you heal the veins, so as to stop up the course of the blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and then it also makes a three-edged and beaked awl when it is put on the wound; if it is too large, then it splits gently when it is put on.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there comes a big abscess, which often comes, moreover when it is not healed only once or twice but when the opening of the vein is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	If you hurry, and put on the bed a wet sponge of water and of linen a little warm, and hold it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and you must do this after the flow of blood from a vein, and if it remains in place for several days without any bruising or discoloration, then it does not harm him;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, put on any thing of aloe or myrrh made into a juice of calamus, or mirrhe, or some sort.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there is incision and appearance in the site of the basilica: then put your hand on it, and if you find the place soft to the pressure of the hand, that is the appearance of evil.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat everyone with the amount of medicine that matches his virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it run until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And for those who are sick and need bloodletting, make the wound larger, and let the flames be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and to those who are weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to cure them little and often, and they must be cured by cutting across, not by stabbing;
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this way of curing is saved from the decay of blood and the severing of nerves, and it is better than the long cure or the broad cure.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And to those whose course requires curing, it is necessary to give moist wine in pomegranate juice; if they are heated, if they have a strong smell of blood.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if it is of a cold complexion, if before the cure moist wine is given in muscatel syrup, or in honey syrup aromatized with spices, as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if it arrives at the head, after the flow of blood, it is appropriate that he hums a brew of wine, and a subtle scented syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use other things that we have said in the division or paste of syncope for the evacuation of a vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he vomits up his stomach contents, and sometimes gets better again, but it is appropriate, when it is weakened by great pain, that he heal little by little, according to the quantity of its continuous virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he vomits up his stomach contents after the first pain, and he is very strong, but he heals after .vij hours after the first pain, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who is to be healed on another side, if it is necessary to heal him the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For he has blood accumulation within the body which is already warmed and brings fever. If so, there is a need to extract large quantities and widen the breach as much as possible with small blows on the bone;
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	then you should treat all the conditions for healing, and put your hand on his pulse as it heals, so that death does not come from the hole;
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and if this happens many times, when the healing is neglected;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not right when you see the arm dislocated, and make the blood come out a second time, and the hole is closed, that you press firm upon it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	if he is broken, that he extends the arm carefully, for that would be bad;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let it be until the second time he heals; or you put to the tip of the flame as long as the blood that is frozen to the hole of the vein comes out;
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and place on it a little of salt water, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the wound is infected, let it alone and do not bind it, as long as the abscess is subsiding.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity requires drawing out the blood a second time, whether it is in the same vein or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein under the arm is drawn out at the arm's base, not at its tip, because it is composed of a different nature.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of drawing out the blood so is that the patient holds his hand in warm water until it turns red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then cut it off with a sharp knife, so that the vein appears clearly, then tie it now with a knot, not wide nor long.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	And let the wound open widely, and heal it well near the joint of the hand, and do not draw it out, but put the hand in warm water, and leave the blood running in the water, as long as you have enough of it.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	And if it is cold, do not put the hand in warm water, for one puts it in more in winter than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the healing of this vein is safer than any other vein, since it does not have an artery or a nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The salvation of the right hand is good for all liver diseases, and it is as follows:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Draw out the hand, and dip it in hot water until the vein has gone, if you can see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and bend it across, and cut it all off, if it doesn't hurt anything;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and don't cut too much in the middle, because the nerve are very thin all the way down;
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put back the hand in hot water, it is not unwrapped from the wound, and cannot be taken out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as necessary, if you put oil and thread to sew it firmly together, and do the same for each arm.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The surgeon should then go to the left side of the patient and make an incision, following the path of the disease, and do the same on the right side as I have told you.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The surgeon should then go to the left side of the patient and make an incision along the spine, following the path of all the diseases that are located below the corset.
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	As for the diseases of the mare's milk, and retention of flowers, and disease of the kidneys, and of the cubs and old legs, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of his health is such that the patient drinks some warm water, and rubs the vein until it stops.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and rub the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot go many veins;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you treat it with fire, so that the skin is burned off and the wound is clean; and let the flame go out.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if he cannot get it out, put the foot in water, and let the vein bleed well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if you treat it for the first time, start the second time above a little, because the leg is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not doubt about the nerves, as we have said, and do the same for the other foot evenly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The legs of the sciatic vein are at the ankle, and its sap is the pain in the thigh, when it is for blood heat.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of this sap is that the patient goes or bath, and pulls out from the ankle .iii. days in twisting,
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	For otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, so that you can put your finger on all sides, and crossing;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and worth more than you can imagine, because the leg is out, and it is very red when it is moved by hand.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not heal it, neither does any rain of him who opens or closes the foot, and towards the little day, and keep away from the wells.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and do so much to the blood that you see, and then loosen the ligature, and put cotton on it and tie it up; now he is healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Wound suction with a pump
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Vacuum wounds with a pump are made from horns, or bronze, or glass; and vacuum therapy is performed in one of two ways: by injuring and drawing out blood, or without injuring.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this ventilation which is not to hurt if so .ij. ways: or it is all fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and ventilation that is made by hurting and by extraction of blood if made in .xiiij. parts of the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	of which one is all at the top of the body; and others are in the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and .ij. others on .ij. sides of the neck; and the windpipe is above the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the vacuum of the shoulders; and the vacuum above the hips;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the vacuums of the arms; and the vacuums of the legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the vacuums of the ankles; and the vacuum treatment does not work for big veins, but only for small ones that are scattered throughout the body.
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and therefore do not try this on anyone who has a large vein, as you would with a small one.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not necessary that it be anesthetized, or with any fire or heat, in any disease that comes from over-fullness, until the whole body is voided.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if for necessity of disease it is necessary to vaporize, or by habits, if we anesthetize each hour in the beginning of the month, or at the end, and vomit and in each period;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	For there are those who, when they need to vaporize, become very heavy;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and if there are those who have repulsion and blush in their face, and in their hair, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who drink a drop of blood in their mouth, and have fled the tongue, and thirst for blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if there are such who dream, and see nothing but blood and nausea and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we saw these signs, and especially when it is nearly midnight, we order that you should not breathe for 3 hours.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The saint of music helps with the headache in the head ... that comes to the eyes, and does not come except after the evacuation of all the body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this ventilation if it is in place of the blood of the cerebral,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	nor does it concern anyone of cold complexion who uses it, or who has had a fever, for that does them great harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and therefore it does not concern anyone who is ill with a cold or who has recently had a fever;
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who are recovering from such an illness often become confused, and for that reason the fire cautery should be placed a little further down by the doubt of confusion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The wind-sucking enters the throat at the tip of the tongue and because of this it goes towards the extraction of the bone.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and in splitting the channel of the palm, and all, and filling;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it is necessary to push it back, because if it holds too firmly, then by chance or stomach or body.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The wind-sucking causes three pains in the neck: one at the tip of the tongue, and another at the throat, and another at the roots of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and is in the place of the shrine of the basilica; and it comes that you command to the saint that he expresses his hand to put, that he does not grasp the artery, and does not come running with blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The winds from the north bring with them diseases of the mouth and decay of the gums, and similar diseases that come to the mouth; and they are in the place of the shrines of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The winds from the shoulders bring with them a disease that comes from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The winds from the neck bring as much as from the three veins of the arms,
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	For blood draws from these large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	And command the surgeon not to sew it too tightly, for the vein is bare of hair and can easily split the skin and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup that is on the back so fits well to the foundation, and to the abscesses, and it must be large and of iron, for its work is to milk well; and perhaps, if it were too thin, it would break; and it would make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The suction cups on the legs so easily open, for they draw blood from all the body, and are good for old pains of the joints, and of the toes, and of the bladder, and remove flowers; and they are in the place of the .ij. sophenes, and of the .ij. cheeks, and moreover they weaken the body after long use, and bring about many diseases.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	Here is the translation of the text line-by-line into English:
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	"And if the wound is large, then you must cut it twice: first to open up the deep part of the wound with a sharp instrument."
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	"And if the wound is very thick, then you must cut it three times; and when we want to extract the arrow point by point, we must only pull lightly once."
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	"And if we want to extract the arrow from the wound, then let's do it often; and if the wound is thick, then we must pull hard, and the end should be that the arrow comes out suddenly,"
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and cover with those who have thick skin and tough, that you oil the wells of the suckers of oil-opening and dissolving:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in this state, of oil purple, or of oil of sweet almonds, or of oil of seed of melon;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in the state of a goat, of oil of sorrel, or of lilies, or of chamomile, or other thing.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the surplus is thick and cold, then take oil of almonds, or of balsam, or of fennel, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if one has a sore that is tender and swollen, then there is no need to put oil on it.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it should be washed after the inhalation of red water, or cold water, or water of mulberry, or water of cucumber, or porcelain water, or other similar water.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And if one has moisture, if it rises like this, or with water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And if one has large excesses, they rise with old wine, or water of oak, or a decoction of fennel or chamomile, or other similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and is not suitable to go into a tub before the bath or take a bath; but after the bath an hour or two and does not sleep after the ventilation,
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is necessary that he warm up, when he should be ventilated and when he has been ventilated.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And guard against those who are coleric, and whose blood is too hot and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if he prunes cold things, like pomegranates, endives, lettuce, and mint, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and also small fish, and a chariot with wheels, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those with a cold complexion, if they drink honey syrup, and fragrant wine that is between old and new, and small fish and birds and pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and let him drink more than he eats when he becomes winded;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give to some men three times or four times a day before or after the wind, to strengthen the main members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and be careful with the sun, but it is good for those who are hot to drink water.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The leech that is used to hurt is that which is put on the liver, and the midge, and the podagra, and on the belly and the bowels and the rain and the hound, for that member does not suffer to be hurt on the skin,
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and do not make it except to attract blood from one member to another,
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	as we put on the breasts when the baby is sick; for the viscosity that is in the member, as we put on leeches on the belly and the bowels to ease the member;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and bone the pain, when there is an operation or stone, if by its virtue it attracts the operation, or deserts the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and so does this, when you put it on the liver and on the mouse when there is repressed wind,
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these suction cups are emptied only for sucking; and never are they together empty, and never is there a plainness of water,
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	as such as the diseases of the lungs, and in this way one fills the suction cup with hot water, or with water in which he has cooked herbs suitable for this;
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction cup is administered to fire thus:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it should be 3 inches wide and half a palm long, and it should have a small hole in the center about as big as a needle is inserted into
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and it should be of brass, smooth before so that it does not hurt the patient when put on the member;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and it has in the middle a crossbar of brass or iron, to put a candlestick between
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and let there be great and small ones according to the diseases and the age of those who take them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For the suction cups of children are different from those of old people, and those of the thin from those of the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And this suction cup must be placed on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	take the wax candle or .i. liquid, and put it in the center of the suction cup at the base of the member that is placed in the center of the suction cup,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the clarity is at the bottom of the suction cup so that it does not burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the member, and your two are on the hole that we have said, so that when you see it, if there is steam, and then take off the suction cup;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and take the lining away as before, and restart it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the suction cup that is adapted for pleurisy, with all water, there is no thread or hole, and it is only adapted when it is flat with water, and put on the member only slightly;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	are not opened except in limbs where it is impossible to put a suction cup because of their smallness, as in the mouth and gums, and similar parts;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in bare legs, if there are two or three toes, and other similar things;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of use so that when you find suction cups that are in clear, non-muddy water, if you take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them in a sweet water nut, as long as they are familiar and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then be cleaned from the vein and the suction cup, and then rub the limb until it is red, and put on the poultices;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are clear, and they cheer up, if it is possible to put a suction cup there, you put it there, because this is worth trying again later;
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If that doesn't work, then lift the head up from there, and then dip it in water, very well, and then squeeze it out;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if he leaves it too long after the heart of the saplings, so that moisten .i. a linen sheet in cold water and put on it, until the sap is dried up;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if there are many saps, then put on them crushed vitriol or scurvy and similar things, until they are dried up;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put on half of boiled peas, and leave them until they burn at the heat, so now they will be dried up;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you have more work to do, then take other saplings.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the blood does not want to come out, so rub the place of the vein with fresh blood, or you put an needle into it as long as there is blood out.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then place them on, and soon as they feel the pain, so they become numb;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are crying, so powder on a little aloes and rosewater, or ash, if they will now stop.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	The chapters of this treatise are many times necessary in the art of medicine, and are the restoration of broken bones and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know this, dear son, that the wise men never wrote of this chapter, nor did they read any letter or book about it;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason the science is strange to us in our land, for I have never found any good book about it;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing, except that by the science of ancient books, from which I have studied so much and treated the science, and by experience, and by the custom of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	and I have described to you in this chapter the contents of the balm, and have summarized it at the end, and have clearly set forth the forms of the tools that are prepared, as I did in the previous twenty chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore appropriate that we say in this book the summary of the words and the chapters where the mind of man takes refuge and stays on truth, so that those who are proven can learn and teach this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when there is a fracture or dislocation or torsion or strain in any part of the body, it is necessary that you hurry to save the sick person from both sides, unless something prevents it from happening, as weakness of the trunk, or paralysis, or age;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if the tension is too great or too frequent; and mild cold winds, and a carriage made of wood and leather, and do not drink wine, nor drink any fatty foods, and do not fill the joints with food, until you have no doubt about the aphorism, nor about the expansion of matter in the member; if the disease returns to its first government that it has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that the patient be nourished with meat that is very fattened, or viscous like cooked wheat, and rice, and peas, and cakes of milk, and oil, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with very fat meat the break is repaired more quickly and sooner.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that broken bones of the old and the infirm cannot be repaired or strengthened according to their nature by the heat of the members, nor those which are too soft, as the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but do not cure, repair on the broken bone. i. large tender meat that hardens and joins the member together, as much as it is necessary; and do not at all cure it with thin meat, and for this reason we have said that it is necessary to feed it with thick meat.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that breakers are many and varied in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the head is another than the break of the leg, or of the arm, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of breaks.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a break that goes up, and another that goes down, as when the blade of a pen is sharpened to write.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break that makes a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each has his own way of preparing it, and its own instrument for restoration, according to what the memory comes in its place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and is cured by turning the bone, and opening it well from both sides, and pressing it with the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no torsness or twiste in the bone, and the patient feels no great pain, it is not broken;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it may have torsness, or a crack, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not necessary for you to move it with your hand, but put on medicine that comes later, and then hold it now gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the break that has come in the shoulder, and there are the three parts separated, it is now necessary to put them together equally, so that the abscesses come forward.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if the abscesses come forward, so that the shoulder is at rest for a day or two, as long as the abscesses are calm.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then put it together equally with the medicine that you can use easily and cleanly, and know that the restoration of the shoulder is easier than the restoration of that which has pieces; then hold it, as it comes later.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are pieces broken, if it is four parts, it is hand or foot, or with your hand a small member, or with four strings, or with one string and with your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and set the member according to its natural form, so that when the parts of the broken member are healed, you remove all additions from their places as much as possible, and keep so that by your work there is no injury or pain for the patient;
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and set well together the two bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well by the hand if it seems to you that it is not yet right: if the dressing is done well and does not come off too much, do not press it so much as those who work with fire and contraction at the member, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limbs are set in place, instruct the patient that he not move them, neither while waking nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and guard well that the limbs be so secure that they feel no pain at all.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when one feels no pain, then it is set in place, and the disposition to move must be such that one feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and guard well that it be placed correctly, so that there is no tortuosity when it is reset.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken member is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	I know that broken members are diverse in smallness and greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small members, such as arms and legs and resembling things: it is necessary to wrap linens of molls and subtle ones.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those that are thick, such as feet and legs: it is necessary to wrap a wide and sturdy linen, for the wide linens embrace all of the large member, and constrain it evenly from all sides, so that there is no stain.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then he stooped lightly, 2 or 3 times or according to the member, and tightened his hand a little at all the joint, then went up over the fracture and tightened it less, so that the fracture then moves a little away from the fracture.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the joint a little and a little, until you press much of the sound place, then take again .1 other joint and turn in chief over the broken place;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then go back to the sound part of the fracture, and tighten it a little way, not too strong or too lightly, as we have said in the first step above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then put between the light joints of linen or drapes, until it is all even, then lay it all above .1 bend, and then put your well-made splints on, if there is an abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is an abscess or an inflammation, place on it a warm thing to soothe the inflammation and let it remain like that for some days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then extract it from your joints, and let them be half a foot long, or from a pole that is used to make cleats, or from palm fronds, and let them be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the stake that one puts on the fracture is a little larger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be as long as necessary for the member, whether small or large;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then hold it on the staples also as you did at first, then tie up one side with a thread going forward, like in the first case on the breach.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	then make it narrower again, less so; and let the thread be fine, not too thick nor too thin, and let it be made of wool;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the thread is too thick, as I would want for works of the fools who make string-like ropes with linden wood, and that is a great mistake, because the ligature cannot be even if it is too thin, and it only deserves to have between each staple half the distance of two inches.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is pricked by the staples of the joints after they have been stripped, then he should be wrapped in linen, or woollen cloth, so that he does not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the bruise, and the cure is broken, I will tell the cure hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not good to extract all the members of a broken body on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the members are large, it is not good to put on stirrups before 2-3 days or more according to the severity of the abscess, especially if hot;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and here is the way of the ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: and it is that you take flour so that it holds the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of egg, and put this confect, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way of the plasterer restoring the fracture to various dispositions, especially for women and small children, for it is not good to be too fine or too rough.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Autre maniere d'emplastre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. Z.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. Z.; acaice vi. Z.; bolic armenic .x. Z., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d'uef, et l'aministre.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Autre manière d’emplastre qui vaut à desévrez de leurs lues, et apaise la douleur soudainement, et le taille utilisent de l’os, et la briseure : pren lainne novele, et la moille en aissile et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cet emplastre ne restaure miie, mais il est bon pour apaiser d’apostème chaud, et ostre proprement les douleurs.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plastering broken bones: take dried fig leaves and earth-p avol leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another method of plastering broken bones and to reduce the remaining swelling at the root of the aposteme. Take roots of mallow, chamomile, violets, timothy grass, each in equal parts; grind them together, and confound them with wine, and heat the limbs, then confound them with coriander seed water, or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another method of plastering broken bones, which is more effective than the first one, when the swelling at the root of the member comes to rest. Take roots of mallow and linseed, borage, melilot, and marsh mallow, and violets and chamomile, each in equal parts; grind them together, and confound them with salt water, or sweet water, or wine, according to the heat of the limb and its need for rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Ypocras states that for the restoration of a broken member, one should not put anything but wax and oil on it, and nothing else; he also says that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galien says that we must put hot things on the broken member to restore it, dry things, as mirr, aloes, incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to make plasters which is useful for lesions and pain: take wool or hair of the same size, or feathers of birds, and bone marrow, and yarn evenly, and grind them, and make a plaster with it and lay it on him.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then let him lie a little while, and take care that the patient feels no pain, or that his bones do not move from their places; but let him lie by day.
